In the next few minutes, you'll learn not only to understand this conversation, but to take part in it yourself. Imagine an American man sitting next to a Frenchwoman. He wants to begin a conversation so he says, "Excuse me?" 
[Male Speaker]
Pardon? 
[Narrator]
The French speaker is going to repeat this word part by part, starting from the end. You are to repeat each part after him, trying to make your pronunciation sound exactly like his. Be sure you repeat aloud.

[Male Speaker]

[Male Speaker]
Anglais.
[Narrator]
Now, again with the "L" sound.
[Male Speaker]
L'Anglais.
[Male Speaker]
L'Anglais.
[Narrator]
The difference is that when the "L" sound is off, you're saying "English", and when it's on, you're saying "the English". Most of the time the "L" sound will be there in French, even when the word the is not there in our language. Once again, say "English".
[Male Speaker]
L'Anglais. 
[Male Speaker]
L'Anglais.

[Male Speaker]

Now, you are to have a conversation with a bellboy in a Paris hotel. You've sent him to get a newspaper for you, giving him a one-hundred franc note. He has now returned and you are arguing with him. [Narrator]
"And I went to Marseille yesterday."
[Female Speaker]
Et je suis allé à Marseille hier. 
[French Narrator]
Demandez-lui si elle est allée à Nice ce matin. 
[Male Speaker]
Est-ce que vous êtes allé à Nice ce matin? 
[Male Speaker]
Est-ce que vous êtes allé à Nice ce matin? 
[Narrator]
And how does he ask, "and when did you arrive?" 
[Male Speaker]
Et quand est-ce que vous êtes arrivé? 
[Male Speaker]
Et quand est-ce que vous êtes arrivé? 
[Male Speaker]
Vous êtes arrivé quand? 
[Narrator]
"When did you arrive in France?" 
[Male Speaker]
Quand est-ce que vous êtes arrivé en France? 
[Male Speaker]
Quand est-ce que vous êtes arrivé en France? 
[Narrator]
"We arrived yesterday." 
[Female Speaker]
Nous sommes arrivés hier. 
[Female Speaker]
Nous sommes arrivés hier. 
[Narrator]
"We are going to remain."
[Female Speaker]
Nous allons rester. 
[Narrator]
"One week."
[Female Speaker]
Une semaine. 
[Narrator]
"And we're going to leave."
[Female Speaker]
Et nous allons partir. 
[Female Speaker]
Et nous allons partir. 
[Narrator]
"We are going to leave tomorrow morning."
[Female Speaker]
Nous allons partir demain matin. 
[Female Speaker]
Nous allons partir demain matin. 
[Narrator]
"We spoke French."
[Female Speaker]
Nous avons parlé français. 
[Narrator]
"We went to Paris."
[Female Speaker]
Nous sommes allés à Paris. 
[Female Speaker]
Nous sommes allés à Paris. 
[Narrator]
We went to -
[French Narrator]
- "Notre-Dame" - 
[Narrator]
- yesterday. 
[Male Speaker]
Nous sommes allés à Notre-Dame hier. 
[Narrator]
I went to -
[French Narrator]
- "Notre Dame."
[Female Speaker]
Je suis allé à Notre-Dame. 
[Female Speaker]
Je suis allé à Notre-Dame.

"With my husband."
[Female Speaker]
Avec mon mari. 
[Narrator]
We went to -

- "Notre Dame" -
[Narrator]
- together. 
[Male Speaker]
Nous sommes allés à Notre Dame ensemble. 
[Male Speaker]
Nous sommes allés à Notre Dame ensemble. 
[French Narrator]
Essayez de dire -
[Narrator]
- "And we ate in a good restaurant."
[Female Speaker]
Et nous avons mangé dans un bon restaurant. 
[Female Speaker]
Et nous avons mangé dans un bon restaurant. 
[French Narrator]
Dites -
[Narrator]
"We ate at the restaurant Chez Pierre."
[Female Speaker]
Nous avons mangé au restaurant Chez Pierre. 
[Narrator]
"It's a very good restaurant."
[Female Speaker]
C'est un très bon restaurant. 
[Female Speaker]
C'est un très bon restaurant. 
[French Narrator]
Demandez -
[Narrator]

[Male Speaker]
Où est Chez Pierre? 
[Narrator]
"On Saint-Jacques Street."
[Female Speaker]
Rue Saint-Jacques. 
[Female Speaker]
Rue Saint-Jacques. 
[Narrator]
Now listen to this French conversation. You should now be able to understand the entire conversation. 
[Male Speaker]
Bonjour. Comment allez-vous? 
[Female Speaker]
Je vais très bien. Et vous? 
[Male Speaker]
Moi aussi, je vais très bien. 
[Female Speaker]
Quand est-ce que vous êtes arrivé? 
[Male Speaker]
Je suis arrivé hier avec ma femme. Et ce matin, nous sommes allés à Notre-Dame. 
[Female Speaker]
Est-ce que vous voudriez dîner avec moi ce soir? 
[Male Speaker]
Oui. À quelle heure? 
[Female Speaker]
À 8 heures. 
[Male Speaker]
Oui, d'accord, à 8 heures. Et merci beaucoup. 
[Female Speaker]
Au revoir. À ce soir. 
[Male Speaker]
À ce soir. 
[Narrator]
This is the end of Unit Thirty, the last unit of level one. The next CD, CD number sixteen, contains all of the reading texts of the course. You may have already begun the readings along with the units. If you have not completed the readings, you should now proceed to the reading text CD. You will need your reading booklet to use in conjunction with the CD. Full instructions are contained on the CD. If you have been able to answer correctly approximately 80% of the questions you've been asked to respond to in this course, you are now ready to go on to level two. To continue to learn your new language, please contact us. This has been a Simon & Schuster audio presentation.
